In this graph, I reversed the symptoms with their opposites, so as to get a more positive spin.</div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><span><br /></span></span></div>It\'s hard to keep a straight face when asked by someone, "and what <i>are</i> his symptoms?" <br /><br />My response is likely something like, "h</span>ow do you want them categorized?"</span><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br />So here, the numbers are "the higher the better." There is no cure. There is only symptom management. Florence Nightingale had ME/CFS, and still there is no cure, and few studies.&nbsp;</span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Severe Fatigue all the time</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Cognitive challenges, especially memory, strategic and divergent thinking</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">High risk of P.E.M.E. (a worsening of symptoms after negative or positive exertion). disorders</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">No appetite, ever -- has to eat on a schedule</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">ADL (Activities of Daily Living) require Disorders</span></h3><div><span style="font-family: arial;">These are not traditional insomnia.</span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: Neuralgia</span></h3><div><span style="font-family: arial;">This illness has episodes of symptoms that become more frequent and intense over time. They usually occur on one side of the face. In Mike\'s case, it\'s his left side.</span></div><span style="font-family: arial;"><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Episodes of severe, shooting or jabbing pain that feels like an electric shock</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Off and on painful headache with intense pain for about 30 seconds at a time, then recurring. </span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">It feels like something burning being inserted in the left ear and gradually spreading to left cheek and jaw before subsiding.</span>&nbsp;</li></ol></span><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Summary</span></h3></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Any of these categories might be subcategories of his ME/CFS, or they could each be a separate set of symptoms caused by the Long Covid. I\'ll get back to that in a minute.</span></span></div></div><div class="x1e56ztr" data-block="true" data-editor="1irgn" data-offset-key="66hmp-0-0" style="background-color: white; color: #050505; margin-bottom: 8px; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="66hmp-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><span data-offset-key="66hmp-0-0"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">As I\'ve shouted from the rooftops, Mike is not yet turning a corner on "getting better." There\'s a chasm between treating symptoms and actually recovering. \n\nAs for crossing that chasm, Mike and I will know it when we\'re there. We\'ll tell you when we think he has started "getting better."</span></span></div></div><div class="x1e56ztr" data-block="true" data-editor="1irgn" data-offset-key="dcfqj-0-0" style="background-color: white; color: #050505; margin-bottom: 8px; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="dcfqj-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><span data-offset-key="dcfqj-0-0"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">In his illness for the last fourteen months, what he does get is a bit of variation from one day to next in which symptoms are high and which symptoms are lower.  He has spikes, it\'s largely unpredictable, and the fatigue never drops.\n\nSince last summer, he has also had an overall slightly lowered incidence of a few of the neuropsychiatric symptoms (which is a subset of all his symptoms) and the reason for the slightly lowered incidence of those few is because we are masking them with psychotropic medications. Masking is not recovering but it helps make life more liveable.\n\nIn the meantime, we\'ve trying other strategies in the hopes of lowering various symptoms or at least quelling those spikes.  We ultimately want to kick-start an actual recovery, but that might have to happen on its own, as we now know from at least one study that ME/CFS, when caused by the Covid-19 virus specifically, can resolve in some sufferers (unlike the ME/CFS symptoms caused by other viruses.)\n \nIf you understand basic probability, and consider that much of what he\'s experiencing is essentially random, it\'s not a shock that he could have a day in which almost all the symptoms are at their best (not gone but best) on the same day.\n\nIt happened today. Let me make it clear we are far from believing that he\'s turning the corner toward actual recovery. Rather, this is a probability event. \n\nThe miracle of it is that it happens to coincide with a plan he had for today that was ridiculous for him to try and do, but we made that decision judiciously, as it would be too much of a hit to his mental health to skip it. \n\nWe knew there was an excellent chance he would have to force his way through today and be a wreck. It has happened before, so trust this: there is no correlation between his plan to do something "normal" today and his planetary lineup.\n\nI have a background in math, I understand statistics and probability, I graph his correlations, and I also understand when good stuff happens by the grace of the universe. They all co-exist, and every day, I am discerning the differences. Until I see more correlations, today is an anomaly in terms of his illness but also a gift from above.</span></span></div></div><div class="x1e56ztr" data-block="true" data-editor="1irgn" data-offset-key="du1cv-0-0" style="background-color: white; color: #050505; margin-bottom: 8px; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="du1cv-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><span data-offset-key="du1cv-0-0"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">And so, off he went to his big annual event. And just for today, I have a spring in my step. I take what I can get.\n\nCautiously, I\'ll add this -- one or two of those symptoms could have been mitigated by a change we just made this week in one of his treatments, but certainly not all the symptoms are quelled by that one adjustment. And it\'s too early to tell whether there\'s any correlation at all.</span></span></div></div><div class="x1e56ztr" data-block="true" data-editor="1irgn" data-offset-key="b6gs5-0-0" style="background-color: white; color: #050505; margin-bottom: 8px; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="b6gs5-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><span data-offset-key="b6gs5-0-0"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">Mike\'s condition today is what\'s known formally in the field of probability as a "rare event" or in statistics, an "outlier." \n\nIt\'s still not a truly good day, either, as his fatigue level is as high as it always is.  He has to be careful to pace himself today, as always. But the upside is he\'s going to be with friends, and  will be able to have ffffffffun because of this anomaly.\n\nI am certain that those of you familiar with this illness will understand what I just wrote. And those who intuitively understand statistics and probability can understand it too. And, lastly, those of you who apply themselves to believing me will also catch on to all the nuances.\n\nSo if you got all the way to the end, thank you. My report had to be this long, because to omit the nuanced details only leads to overgeneralizations and false conclusions. Us Long Covid survivors deal with overgeneralizations and false conclusions every day, and it\'s alienating.\n\nTo come up to the surface, there\'s a parallel here -- scientific discovery takes a long time. font-size: medium;">Aside from all the other Long Haul Covid symptoms, Mike has four sleep disorders -- all four of which are directly caused by the condition of Long Covid and ME/CFS, and are not a side effect of any medication, as we have ruled that out.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;"><span>Major:&nbsp;<b>Sleep onset delay</b> also called<b> sleep latency<br /><br /></b></span><span>We are on the warpath to find answers to this, but the experts don\'t know either, and we see no strong correlations yet.<br /><br />Along with some other remedies, Mike does a nightly dose of tart cherry juice. Tart cherry juice contains melatonin and tryptophan, and it\'s an antiflammatory. Without his nightly dose, his&nbsp;</span><b>sleep latency</b><span>&nbsp;might be worse.&nbsp;&nbsp;<br /><br /></span></span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">Major:&nbsp;<b>Non-restorative sleep, </b>also called<b> unrefreshed sleep</b><br /><br />Non-restorative sleep has been studied and is currently being studied, with a handful of theories in mind. Recently, evidence seems to be pointing toward autonomic dysfunction. Non-restorative sleep is known to be a hallmark of ME/CFS. See this&nbsp;<a href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/29770505/" target="_blank">NIH report</a>. This condition is one cause of memory problems, so it could explain Mike\'s memory problems.<br /><br />We think that this past week and a half, after son David\'s medical issues, Mike\'s having a bout of PESE, which is presenting as this more days than usual of non-restorative sleep.<br /><br /></span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">Major: <b>Long Sleeping<br /></b><br />He sleeps ten to twelve hours a night. Longer sleep doesn\'t refresh.<br /><br /></span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">Minor:&nbsp;<b>Night waking&nbsp;</b><br /><br />Mike\'s night waking is rare but is a symptom of ME/CFS. It is common with ME/CFS for some symptoms to come and go with seemingly no explanation. I am then keeping a graph, as I\'ve done in the past for other correlation-seeking. My efforts have been largely futile until possibly now.</div><div><br /></div><h4 style="text-align: left;">At last, I may have found a connection!</h4>No, I still don\'t see a correlation in the graph, but I may have found a trigger, which wasn\'t getting reported daily and hasn\'t been in the graph.<br /><br />So now, we will have to go back into:<br /><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Anecdotal data, which we can find sporadically mentioned in our document</span></li><li>Past events in our google calendar</li><li>Any anecdotal data Mike may have been writing into his "Visible" phone app</li></ol></span><h4 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">The trigger could be EXERTION</span></h4><span style="font-family: arial;">We do know that social, cognitive, emotional and physical exertion can lead to Post Exertional Symptom Exacerbation. It\'s a mouthful, but its abbreviation is PESE. (It used to be called PEM.)</span><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Months ago, Mike has a big attack of PEM that lasted a few weeks. It was the result of trying to push through (because no doctor told us not to because no doctor was willing to diagnose the ME/CFS -- that\'s an egregious topic for another day, another post.)</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><h4 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Here\'s my theory</span></h4><div><span style="font-family: arial;">As a result of that weeks-long PESE episode, Mike knows how to pace himself now. However, there are more minor exertions that could be leading to his sleep onset delay. After all, exertion isn\'t black and white.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">The problem could be accumulation of small exertions, or it could be just one type of exertion. I don\'t know. I would theorize that physical exertion is the least of the culprits.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><h4 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">And the resulting symptom? Maybe the SLEEP ONSET DELAY</span></h4><div><span style="font-family: arial;">I think it could be that his days of a little more exertion, while not leading to the very extreme PESE he had many months ago, could be leading to just one symptom -- his sleep onset delay.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Alternatively, the resulting symptom could be the "waking unrefreshed." Happily, we are measuring all the energy symptoms already. <br /><br />Moving forward, I think I want to write down each day some way of quantifying his exertion of the day before (and its type) so it\'s all in one place.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">In the meantime, the project ahead of me is to scrape up past exertions, and figuring out how to quantify them.<br /><br /><br />_________________________________________________________<br /><br /> Join my  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/longcovidmind">Long Covid Mind</a> Facebook group. Even for those of us who have been blessed with good doctor care, we still need the assurance that something is being done in the background. It is. \n\nThe medical researchers are scrambling to figure this thing out. We need to stay forward thinking, as best we can.</span></div><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="b24fk-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><span data-offset-key="b24fk-0-0" style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><h4 style="position: relative; text-align: left;"><span data-offset-key="b24fk-0-0" style="font-family: arial;">The goodness about the ongoing studies:</span></h4><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="b24fk-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">The funding is now there</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Studies are being done from all angles</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">A lot more is known now about Long Covid than three years ago</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Researchers learned a lot from figuring out HIV -- this Long Covid research could happen a lot faster than the HIV studies</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Now we have Machine Learning (a common and efficacious kind of Artificial Intelligence) combined with EHR\'s (Electronic Health Records) which will hasten all of the research </span></li></ol><h4 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Great, but now what?</span></h4></div><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="b24fk-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><span style="font-family: arial;">We\'re hanging our hats on waiting for the research, but what to do in the meantime? The short answer is do whatever you can to get help. Here are some thoughts, based on our own experience and that of others.</span></div><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="b24fk-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><span data-offset-key="b24fk-0-0" style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div class="_1mf _1mj" data-offset-key="b24fk-0-0" style="direction: ltr; position: relative;"><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Gather a few medical terms related to your condition. A few examples of terms that could get your doctor\'s attention:\n\n</span></li><ul><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Say PASC instead of Long Covid</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Tell your doctor there\'s a diagnosis code for PASC</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Use the term "neuropsychiatric symptoms" or neuro-PASC</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Keep in mind, doctors are not researchers. They are waiting for the research just as we are. It\'s okay to inform your doctor! (Find gentle ways to do so while protecting their egos.)</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">If you have symptoms of ME/CFS, which is likely, tell your doctor you seem to have a number of symptoms "consistent with" ME/CFS (which used to be called Chronic Fatigue Syndrome.) Doctors like the term "consistent with." </span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">If your symptoms flair after exertion, use the term PESE (which stands for Post Exertional Symptom Exacerbation.) You will likely be ahead of your doctor on this newer term -- your doctor might know it as PEM (Post Exertional Malaise.) </span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Directly ask your doctor if they could do some research for you; for example, to see if they can find a clinical trial you can participate in. Such a request will help prompt your doctor to learn about this condition, even if the outcome is they can\'t find a clinical trial. In other words, find ways to prompt them to want to learn.\n\n</span></li></ul><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Get used to the idea that for now, you need to treat symptoms. Relief is not the same as recovery, but it can really help while waiting. And accept the fact that you may need multiple specialists to treat your symptoms. There is no one doctor for "Long Covid."\n\n</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">If at all possible, do visit a "Long Covid Clinic" sometimes called a "Post Covid Clinic" or PCC. The reason? Your answers to their questions will contribute to the ongoing research. Your data can help find your cure! Get on the waiting list now; these clinics are busy.\n\n</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Find an easy, comfortable way to document for yourself your different symptoms each day, and use whatever kind of scale works for you, to rate the severity of each one. For example, what level is your fatigue today on a scale of 0 to 100? How much dizziness did you have yesterday? It doesn\'t have to be fancy -- you can do this in a journal with a pen. Over time, you might see fluctuations, and be able to track whether your remedies are working.\n\n</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Use your own journaling to help you distinguish between symptoms which you might not otherwise realize are separate. For example, a sleep disorder and fatigue are different. It\'s possible to have a good night\'s sleep and still have fatigue in the morning. That way, you can notice which remedies are working for what. And then you can tell your doctor "I have sleep onset delay and I have fatigue." This kind of specifics will make more of an impression than "I\'m tired all the time."\n\n</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Be open, if possible, to conventional medication for depression, anxiety, psychosis, and other mental health conditions, keeping in mind that these symptoms are caused directly by the virus -- it\'s not all in your head. There are many tried and trusted medications already in existence that can give you the relief you need to at least function, and maybe think cleary and become a better self-advocate.\n\n</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Ask your physician to please look into the existing genetic tests that will help guide decision-making about trying medication. These tests help individualize recommendations for medications to try.\n\n</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">If you\'re easily intimidated by physicians, you might need to get outside your comfort zone a little bit. This one is Part One. We now know that a reinfection of Covid-19 (or even other viruses such as the common cold) could lead to a new, even worse bout of both Covid-19 and of Long Covid (a.k.a. PASC). This would mean:</span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">A worsening of Mike\'s current episodic symptoms</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">An even greater vulnerability to Post Exertional Symptom Exacerbation&nbsp;</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">New symptoms of Covid-19, of which there are over two hundred, and of Long Covid, of which there are dozens more</span></li></ol></div><span style="font-family: arial;"><div>Summarizing some of his 2022 symptoms below, let\'s leave it to the readers\' imaginations what 2023 could look like if these symptoms get worse:</div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li>Severe depression</li><li>Severe anxiety</li><li>Severe fatigue</li><li>Three sleep disorders</li><li>Intrusive thoughts</li><li>Paranoia</li><li>Migraines</li><li>Brain fog&nbsp;</li><li>Sensory overload (music, movies, and even stores can be overload)</li><li>Loss of strategic brain fuctioning</li><li>Loss of memory</li><li>Loss of ability to initiate ideas</li><li>Complete loss of appetite</li><li>Lightheadedness</li><li>Drop in blood pressure and severe fatigue after raising arms (such as when taking showers)</li><li>Emotional flattening</li><li>Concentration problems</li><li>Information processing problems</li><li>Tremors</li><li>Can only work four hours a day</li><li>Severe limitations in his social, mental, and physical exertions</li><li>Secondary symptoms, such as gastrointestinal and other side effects from new medications meant to treat these primary symptoms</li></ol><div>And of course, the above list doesn\'t include all the new symptoms he could get, some of which are deadly.</div><div>&nbsp;</div><h1 style="text-align: left;">The Results could be:</h1><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li>More meds than ever before, which would escalate exponentially the side effects and contraindications, which could in turn, lead to yet more meds</li><li>Hospitalization</li><li>More doctor visits than ever before (raising his risk of further exposure)</li><li>Further reduction of his work hours from part-time to no-time</li><li>Even more drastic changes to our lifestyle</li><li>Complete housebound isolation&nbsp;&nbsp;</li></ol><div>We\'ve met people who are completely housebound, except when in and out of the hospital. I can\'t think of a word that\'s worse than "nightmare."</div></div></div><div><br /></div><span><a name=\'more\'></a></span><div>Join my  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/longcovidmind">Long Covid Mind</a> Facebook group. This post is Part Two. If you read Part One, you\'ll understand why it\'s time for us to take another shot at our Covid safety guidelines.</div><div><br /></div></span><div><span style="font-family: arial;">These new guidelines are a mix of risk/reward ratio, our trust in others, and our mental health.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">There are obviously shades of gray, but to simplify, we can outline three criteria for our travel and visiting decisions:</span><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>Trust in Attitudes:</b>&nbsp;<br />We\'re willing to be around people whom we trust to:<br /></span></li><ul><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Respect this pandemic</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Take Long Covid seriously</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Respect chronic disability</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Be willing to meet the needs of the most vulnerable group member</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Believe us<br /></span></li></ul><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>Trust in Distancing, Masks, and Rules:</b>&nbsp;<br />This allows us to do some amount of engaging one of our greatest joys, which is galavanting around NYC:<br /></span></li><ul><li><span style="font-family: arial;">When on mass transit, we distance and wear masks</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">When outside in NYC, we distance and sometimes wear masks</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">When considering entering inside in NYC, we check on rules and crowdedness, and we do masks and distancing<br /></span></li></ul><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>Ready access to Paxlovid is our security blanket:</b>&nbsp;<br />In the worst case scenario, we know we have quick easy access to Paxlovid or other treatments. Because treatments and providers are still in flux, we\'ve nailed down for ourselves a list of all contacts of whom we will ask this question: "What\'s the fastest way for us to get the best treatment?" That list is sitting where we can see it. <br /><br />This third option allows us to not have to completely isolate.</span></li></ol><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Why attitudes matter</span></h1><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Our decisions have led to some disappointments, but that\'s life.&nbsp; We\'ve had to close in our circle a little more. That change, we\'ve learned, is not uncommon to people we\'ve met who have Long Covid.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">The upshot is we\'ve had to make some further changes in our lifestyle. This includes less tolerance of ableist attitudes.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">For almost thirty-one years, we\'ve seen precious few abelist attitudes toward our disabled son. Yet in the last year, we\'ve seen ample ableist attitudes toward Long Covid. The difference may have to do with both visibilty and current understanding of the disability. <br /><br />In our son\'s case, his disability shows clearly on his face, and is well understood. In contrast, Mike\'s Long Covid is largely invisible, and is new to the medical community and the community at large.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Abelist attitudes directed right to our faces, such as "I don\'t worry about Covid-19" have no place in our mental health.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We also have no room for folks who think they know better than we do about Mike\'s condition, treatment, meds, our choices, and my needs as Mike\'s caregiver and chief researcher.</span></div><div><br /></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Ultimately, no one can know how best we should pick our battles except us.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We rely on the support from our wonderful family and friends in the form of bolstering, cheering, and open-minded interest. Your current tribe may not be equipped to support your emotional and physical needs. Better yet, find individuals<br /><br /></span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Expect to be criticized -- you\'re either doing too much or not enough, either for yourself, or for your loved one. But I have my limits. It\'s time to make some waves.</span></div><span style="font-family: arial;"><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div>It is unseemly to spread around one\'s own unresearched conclusions or platitudes about this illness. Those in our inner circle, who listen, believe, and care about us, don\'t say these terrible things:</span><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">It\'s two steps forward, one step back</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">It\'s one step at a time</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">It\'s Mike\'s decision when he can emerge</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">That\'s life...stuff happens</span></li></ol><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We don\'t mind lack of understanding. What we mind is folks passing around unenlightened statements.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">So I will lovingly explain:</span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>Two steps foward, one step back</b>&nbsp;suggests he is getting better. He\'s not. Managing symptoms is not the same as "getting better." We can only manage symptoms.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>One step at a time</b> suggests he\'s getting better. He\'s not</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>It\'s Mike\'s decision</b> suggests he has control. The only limited control he has is in how to spend his spoons, and that\'s only on days when he has some spoons to spend</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>That\'s life...stuff happens</b> is unhelpful and callous. This is the <b>love</b> of my life, and I will do everything I can to protect and help him</span></li></ol><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Letting people love you the way they want to love you is a nice idea, and sometimes appropriate. But it doesn\'t fit for us in this circumstance.</span></div></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">It\'s time to make waves. Courtesy doesn\'t always right wrongs. Conflict avoidance doesn\'t always bring about justice. Anger has its place.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Disabled and chronically ill people deserve some understanding and some effort.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Our culture still marginalizes them.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><br /><hr /><span style="font-family: arial;">Join my  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/longcovidmind">Long Covid Mind</a> Facebook group. They can all can lead to&nbsp;Post-Exertional Symptom Exacerbation (PESE). Other forms of stress, such as deadlines or conflicts, also lead to PESE.<br /><br />Existing symptoms such as disabling fatigue or exhaustion, difficulty thinking, pain, exercise intolerance, and other symptoms are made worse by exertion.<br /><br /></span></li><li><b>Get reinfected with Covid-19</b>. A survey showed that reinfection overwhelmingly worsened the symptoms of Long COVID in most people who were still symptomatic.<br /><br />In those who still have Long COVID at the time of reinfection, 80% see their symptoms worsen, and 85% see old symptoms return or new additional symptoms emerge. <a href="https://www.longcovidkids.org/post/a-world-first-effect-of-covid-reinfection-on-people-living-with-long-covid" target="_blank">Click here</a> to find the survey (a downloadable pdf.)<br /><br /></li><li><b>Get a different virus, such as a cold</b>. Patients with Long Covid have reported exacerbation of their Long Covid symptoms after they get the common cold. <br /><br />It\'s possible an infection of other viruses such as Herpes and Epstein-Barr can also excacerbate the symptoms of Long Covid. <br /><br />But what we do know is Covid-19 virus&nbsp;can trigger reactivation of an existing, latent Herpes Virus or Epstein-Barr Virus.<br /><br />We also know that ME/CFS, which embodies the set of symptoms that half of all Long Covid patients develop, existed before Covid-19 did, and is known to be triggered by other viruses, including Herpes and Epstein-Barr.</li></ol><h3 style="text-align: left;">What to do to prevent Exacerbation</h3><div><br /></div><div>As you might have concluded, all three the above-described are forms of stress. So, reduce every kind of stress you can. Specifically:</div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><b>Relentless self-pacing</b>. Limit social, physical, and emotional exertion each day. And if you can get more granular than that, do so. For example, you might need to limit upper body exertion more than limiting your walking.<br /><br /></li><li><b>Masking always</b>. Be counter-culture. Be counter-family. Even if everyone around you has tested negative for Covid-19, just so you can be included, one person with a cold can exacerbate your symptoms.</li></ol></div></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span><hr /><span style="font-family: arial;"><big><span style="font-size: medium;">  Join my&nbsp;\n<a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/longcovidmind">Long Covid Mind</a>&nbsp;Facebook group. The reason is not because it\'s "all in their head."<br /><br />Rather, the reason is that Long Covid can include multiple neuropsychiatric symptoms. Because Long Covid has no cure, we need to treat each symptom. That can mean multiple specialists.</span><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br />A psychiatrist (or a psychiatric&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: arial;">nurse)</span><span style="font-family: arial;">&nbsp;are the specialists who can prescribe those serious meds.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">While all of us can probably benefit from therapy, especially to cope with the current changes in our lives, I\'m guessing there are Long Covid patients who can benefit well enough from the meds, without supplemental therapy.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Conventional wisdom says do both. But Long Covid forces us to pick our battles to an exponential degree. That fact sometimes redefines wisdom.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">And now here\'s another wrinkle, and I draw no conclusions. Rather, it\'s of help for everyone to be aware of in their decision-making. It comes from a University of Cambridge study:</span></div><div style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;"><b>&nbsp;Therapy and meds affect two different parts of the brain!</b></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">From <a href="https://psyche.co/ideas/mental-disorders-are-brain-disorders-heres-why-that-matters?utm_source=Psyche+Magazine&amp;utm_campaign=155bbbbeef-EMAIL_CAMPAIGN_2023_01_17_02_28&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_term=0_-155bbbbeef-%5BLIST_EMAIL_ID%5D">Psyche.co</a>:&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="color: #2d2b29; font-family: Tiempos Text, Georgia, Times, serif;"><span style="background-color: white; font-size: 22px;">&nbsp;</span></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">"The results were striking  there was no overlap between the brain changes from antidepressant medication and those from psychological therapy.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">"Instead, psychological therapy specifically changed brain activation in the medial prefrontal cortex, a region involved in attention and awareness of your emotional state,&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">"...whereas antidepressant medication specifically changed activation in the amygdala, which is more directly implicated in generating emotional states."<br />&nbsp;<br /></span><br /><hr /><span style="font-family: arial;">Join my <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/longcovidmind">Long Covid Mind</a> Facebook group. It has benefits and drawbacks.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Why do we isolate?</span></h3><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Severity of symptoms, including anxiety, prevents visiting&nbsp;</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Concern for reinfection&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">To preserve our fragile and volatile mental health, we avoid people who trivialize, marginalize, deny, and even denigrate the illness</span></li></ol></div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">But we need the support of a few individuals who "get it"&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></h3><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Preserving mental health has to be the highest priority. Without our mental health, we don\'t recover. So we must have support from those few who:</span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Believe us</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Understand that the world is full of misinformation about the illness</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Are willing to trust our research</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Can hear bad news as well as good</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Are on our side</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Can slow down to our pace of recovery</span></li></ol></div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">But that presents a problem</span></h3><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Mixed groups are too painful to be around. Even one dismissive type can cause more distress than it\'s worth to be in that group</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">So here\'s what we did and are doing</span></h3><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We\'ve become relentless about forging existing and new individual relationships, both in person, and online:</span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Writing Mike\'s blog journey and sending out to a mailing list</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Running a Facebook group and participating in another Facebook group</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Meeting with individuals from church and family</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Staying in touch with loved ones who "get it"</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Finding new listening ears</span></li></ol><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">The Results</span></h3></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Individual members of our family, friends, and church are on board</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">We periodically receive messages of prayer, love and concern, and we even received a prayer shawl!</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Our mental health is much better because of our carefully chosen support individuals</span>&nbsp;</li></ol><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">But where to start?</span></h3></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Many Covid patients are not so lucky as us. They have no support at all, not even a siginifcant other to advocate for them. But adding one person to your camp is better than adding zero. Go slow.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">And think outside the box. Your potential support individuals might not be who you think they should be. When I would go fishing as a kid, my dad used to say "the biggest fish are where you find them." So stay open-minded.</span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><span>Instead of thinking in terms of your family or your place of worship, think in terms of one individual at a time.&nbsp;</span>You probably already have wisdom about which folks are better relegated to "fair weather friends."</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">If you have one or two people on your side, let them know they are allowed and encouraged to spread around their knowledge, if they feel so inclined.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Professional help is good too. Therapists, psychiatrists, faith leaders, life coaches. It\'s not their title that counts. It\'s whether you see that they can march in your parade.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Join some online groups. This is a somehwat tricky area, as you might get a bit of negativity, but there\'s so much support on those groups that it could be worth it. And you can report trolls. The haters don\'t stick around long.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Remember to show interest in your support people. One-sided support isn\'t healthy.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">One more thought -- people burn out. It\'s human nature. So, finding new support from time to time can help you. Remember that our illness isn\'t easy to hear about.</span></li></ol></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Here\'s a <a href="https://solvecfs.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/05/Loving-Someone-with-MECFS-or-Long-Covid.pdf" target="_blank">helpful read</a>, written both for the patient and their support.</span></div><div><br /></div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">It takes courage, but that\'s a resource all of us can muster!</span></h3><div><span style="font-family: arial;">No matter the severity of our symptoms, it is my opinion that courage resides in a remaining healthy place in our brains. Remember, courage is a decision that coexists with fear.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Wisdom is the joining of emotion and intellect. Use your wisdom to pick and choose, and be relentless.&nbsp;</span></div><div><br /></div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">But sometimes isolation is the better choice</span></h3><span style="font-family: arial;">I think it\'s safe to say that the majority of folks in our Long Covid community have no perseverence leftover. Thus, it starts to look like support is optional. I\'d say that\'s valid. It has to be. And yes, conventional wisdom needs to be a little flexible.</span><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br />And another reason not to try -- for many, any more rejection is intolerable and therefore unthinkable.</span><div><br /></div><hr /><span style="font-family: arial;">Join my  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/longcovidmind">Long Covid Mind</a> Facebook group. All are welcome and it has a focus toward the mental health and neuropsychiatric symptoms of Long Covid. It is public but you can post anonymously<br /><br />Join my  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/longcovidmindcaregiver">Long Covid Mind Carevigers</a> Facebook group, which is new and private<br /><br />Join the <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/COVID19survivorcorps">Survivor Corps</a> Facebook group, which more heavily addresses all the other physical symptoms. Pick a day. Any day. Those lines represent symptoms.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br />It is my hope that out of everyone asking me about Mike\'s condition, everyone praying, everyone reading my emails, Facebook group, or texts, that there is at least one person who finally believes that Mike is not "getting better." It doesn\'t work that way.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">That\'s because he has a life-long condition that has been known to be caused by a few evil viruses, and now Covid-19 is has plunked itself down on that list.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">He has a condition called ME/CFS. Because there\'s finally pharmaceutical interest.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">And why is there finally pharmaceutical interest? The sheer number of people getting this illness after having a mild case of Covid.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Yes, I said mild case of Covid. The new numbers show that 90% of people living with long COVID initially experienced only mild illness with COVID-19. (See <a href="https://theconversation.com/long-covid-stemmed-from-mild-cases-of-covid-19-in-most-people-according-to-a-new-multicountry-study-195707?utm_source=substack&amp;utm_medium=email" target="_blank">Research Brief</a> for more about this.)</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Here\'s one way to explain how ME/CFS works: It\'s a big bucket of symptoms that have a mind of their own. They come and go as they please, not correlated to any action.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Each patient can have a subset at any one time, and a new symptom can emerge at any time. For most or all the symptoms, no trigger is ever identified.</span></div><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">Mike\'s New Symptom -- Migraine</span></h1><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Mike\'s brand new symptom last night was a migraine. So I looked it up. Yup. Sure enough, that\'s a possible symptom of ME/CFS. It\'s new for Mike. It could return. Or not. There is no pattern to this.</span></div><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">Additional symptoms that returned last night</span></h1><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Jumpy, anxious, heartburn, nausea, dizzy, all preceded last night\'s migraine.</span></div><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">What do we have control over?</span></h1><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Because we can\'t find correlations, we have no control over new symptoms or old symptoms reappearing.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We do have control over preventing symptom exacerbation, also known as PESE (Post Exertional Symptom Exacerbation). That\'s prevented by non-stop mindful pacing, even on the "good" days. Mike is doing pacing beautifully.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">Now look at the graph again</span></h1><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Looking at the graph, imagine other lines appearing in other colors on other days. Some days there are five; some days ten; some days more.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">If even one person replies to me by email, text, comment, phone, or carrier pigeon that you "get it now," I will be so happy.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">I have to find my happiness in strange places.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">So I\'m begging those who love Mike -- please accept that he is not on the mend. It is not easily solved by traditional strategies.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>Mike has suffered for many months with this symptom, leading to waking each day in the afternoon. They undervalue doing their own research, they take&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: arial;">little to no interest in their patient\'s input, they won\'t admit they don\'t know something, and some still denigrate use of the internet -- an outdated notion.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">&nbsp;</span></div><span style="font-family: arial;">As an ME/CFS and Long Covid patient team, Mike and I advocate and research a great deal before visiting any doctor. Your health is more important than your feelings of intimidation.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">If you have felt marginalized by a doctor, you must work on your courage, b</span><span style="font-family: arial;">e insistent, and stay that way for every visit.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">You have more power than you might realize. You can transform them into better doctors for everyone.</span></div><div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We have successfully fast-tracked Mike\'s trek by providing research and ideas.&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: arial;">Here\'s a smattering of examples of us taking the initiative:</span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">We suggested certain changes in his neuropsychiatric meds, to which our doctor was open, and they ended up being the exact right thing for Mike.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">We provided a Long Covid specialist eighteen pages that included Mike\'s Long Covid history, research, and our suggestions. As a result, she was able to ask us much deeper questions than she otherwise would have.&nbsp;</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">After one of our doctors turned down several of our suggestions for OTC alternative remedies, we didn\'t get discouraged. Instead, we continued throwing one or two OTC remedies into our research, and as a result, he did approve one, which we are hopeful about.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Because of the number of doctors we had to communicate with, we eventually realized that his GP, who should have been the one at the helm, was falling behind. So we suggested that she and Mike schedule a standing monthly virtual visit, and she heartily agreed to this.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">One time, when the GP\'s care team tried to send us to the emergency room, we showed them evidence that patients with ME/CFS get these very symptoms often, and we showed them why the ER should be the last resort. As a result, they backed off quickly and found other medically sound alternatives to an ER visit</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">We\'re the ones who suggested CBD or THC to one of our doctors, and when we showed the doctor what we bought, he evaulated our purchases, agreed, and offered suggestions for dosages. We know he would not have independently brought up canabanoids at that time.</span></li></ol><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">But you and doc won\'t always agree</span></h1><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Of course, you won\'t always be right. Your doctor, after all, has a wealth of knowledge.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">After considering our research, we\'ve had doctors sometimes disagree with us and offer a better idea. Here\'s why that\'s just as good an outcome:</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><b><span style="font-size: medium;">We secretly know that when a doctor carefully considers our research first, this leads to a more well-considered next step</span></b></span></div></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><b><br /></b></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">And so, either way, whether the doctor goes with our lead or counters with something else, we are able to genuinely thank them for their help, and we walk out of the office (or virtual office) smiling.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: medium;">Join my  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/longcovidmind">Long Covid Mind</a> Facebook group. This post is about my discovery of how to ask for what I need, and why that\'s especially hard to do when in crisis.</span></div><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">My symptoms</span></h1><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Drained</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Worried</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Have to think for two of us&nbsp;</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Low energy</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Depression</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Anxiety (this is a condition in which the brain sends signals of danger when there is no danger)</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Isolation, due to avoiding covid exposure and difficulty engaging the world</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Naysayers abound, and they\'re disheartening</span></li></ol><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">My Discovery</span></h1><div><span style="font-family: arial;">As trashed as I am, it\'s up to me to figure out what I need. Nobody can do that for me. Here\'s what I figured out:</span></div><div><ol style="text-align: left;"><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Ask specifically for occasional check-ins</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">If folks offer to visit with me, ask them to provide a date, time, and location. That makes a big difference in my ability to say yes (with a special thank you to my SIL modeled this, giving me the idea)</span></li></ol><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">The Results</span></h1></div></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">I am feeling less isolated. And starting to make plans. I guess before this, I felt a littl stuck. I\'m unstuck because I figured out what I need and I said it. It requires vulnerability.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><h1 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">The Upshot</span></h1><div><span style="font-family: arial;">From now on, when someone is going through a crisis, I want to try to be specific about my offers of help.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">That\'s because all crises drain the brain. It\'s what happens to some people, even after a mild case or a silent unknown case, and lasts for months.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>ME/CFS</b> was once known as Chronic Fatigue Syndrome, but the extreme fatigue (which is not sleepiness) is only one part of it, and it\'s now being studied harder and funded better than before the Covid-19 pandemic.</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;"><b>PESE</b> is what happens to people with ME/CFS when they exert themselves. I now have an answer, for anyone who is still, or newly, willing to help.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We understand that we are exhausting, but that\'s the nature of the illness. We\'ll take anybody willing to try. It\'s painful to have people fall away. It\'s painful to get too little support.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><p style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: arial;">If I burn out, that\'s a problem. And truth be told, I\'m starting to feel it. So I\'m probably asking months after I should have.</span></p><div style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Let me shout this: it is so easy to think that someone who has taken on the role of caregiver doesn\'t need help. Caregivers need support, badly.&nbsp;</span></div><div style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: arial;">If I\'ve come across as "I\'ve got this," I don\'t have this.</span></div><div style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: large;"><b>So regardless if...</b></span></div><div><ul style="text-align: left;"><li>You know us well or hardly at all</li><li>You\'v been in touch or not</li><li>You haven\'t known how to help before or want to change how you help</li></ul></div></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: large;"><b>... here\'s how to help&nbsp;</b></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">The most important help I need right now, from anybody willing, is to reach out to me on a regular basis. That can be by text or email or regular reading and commenting on any of my web assets, or a mix of any of this.&nbsp;</span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">This is not an acute illness. It\'s chronic. That means it\'s long-term. That means we burn out our supports. We understand that. We may continue to need a rotation of concern over the coming months (or longer).&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">And it\'s become too hard for us to be the ones reaching out. If you\'ve read about Spoon Theory, we are both limited in our spoons.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: large;"><b><br /></b></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: large;"><b>But if in my response, I ask "and how are you?"...</b></span></div><div style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: arial;">...It doesn\'t mean we\'re fine. Caring about others when I\'m in crisis is part of who I am, and it helps me get outside of myself. So I do want to know, if you\'d like to share.</span></div><div style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: large;"><b><br /></b></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: large;"><b>Alternatively...</b></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial; font-size: large;"><b><br /></b></span></div></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">If you are someone who has been able to keep up with the details in my web assets, and wants to "give it a go" at supplementing my research with an open mind and heart, go for it. Our doctors are flying blind. I am sometimes the one giving us and our doctors direction. It\'s exhausting.</span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">But be kind to me please. And why is it, then, that these few were able to catch on? PEM is a serious setback in ME/CFS recovery.</span></p></div><h2 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></h2><h2 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Here\'s the PEM symptom as described by the CDC:</span></h2><div><span style="background-color: white; font-size: 17px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">People with ME/CFS often describe this experience as a crash, relapse, or collapse. During PEM, any ME/CFS symptoms may get worse or first appear, including difficulty thinking, problems sleeping, sore throat, headaches, feeling dizzy, or severe tiredness.&nbsp;</span></span></div><div><span style="background-color: white; font-size: 17px;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></span></div><div><span style="background-color: white; font-size: 17px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">It may take days, weeks, or longer to recover from a crash. Sometimes patients may be house-bound or even completely bed-bound during crashes. People with ME/CFS may not be able to predict what will cause a crash or how long it will last. As examples:</span></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 17px;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></span><ul style="background-color: white; box-sizing: border-box; font-size: 17px; margin-bottom: 0px; This was not a surprise, as I\'ve met multiple patients on social media who also have been advised to seek physical therapy.<br /><br />Mount Sinai seems to be more oriented toward studies of nuero-PASC than Columbia was, and they appear to be following a cohort, which Mike is now part of. He added that they can help with Mike\'s dizziness, and rebuilding his functioning level. It\'s called "reconditioning." This is not grueling PT by any means. Its purpose is to gently help the brain and body along to slowly heal from the fatigue with no pushing. And it\'s all in a controlled setting.<br /><br />I asked the doctor if Mike could faint during his dizzy spells, as I\'ve read about patients with his condition, fainting with no warning. The doctor said that indeed, Mike could faint.&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: arial;">We\'re watching that closely.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">And Dr. Carnavali concurs with Dr. Parikh and Dr. Galal that Mike must eliminate as many stressful events as possible and that he must pace himself every single day, no skipping. That way he can pace himself hour by hour, which is what he\'s doing while working at home.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">And no more running for the train, either. (Yes I learned the "new math" in school.)</span><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Then, last week...</span></h3><div><span style="font-family: arial;">So last week we went to our first (Columbia Doctors) and you may have read about that in my post. The upshot? We\'re already doing everything, and now we have to wait until the medical community figures out Post Covid Syndrome or until Mike\'s current meds kick in a little more.&nbsp;</span><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Tomorrow...</span></h3></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Tomorrow our Post Covid Clinic is through Mount Sinai. They might have a different focus, and we know they\'re doing specific studies on the neurological effects of Long Covid (neuro-PASC and ME/CFS.) So maybe they\'ll have something more to offer.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Think of it as kind of like the Long Covid version of a second opinion.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We\'ll take prayers, thoughts sent to the universe...anything that could bring out the doctor\'s best wisdom. While it\'s frustrating we had to wait six months, on the flip side, they knew even less than they know now.</span></div></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">As with the last clinic, we are bringing sixteen pages for them to scan.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">The above chart is from a&nbsp;<a href="https://www.healio.com/news/primary-care/20211208/long-covid-symptoms-last-for-more-than-1-year-mount-sinai-study-shows" target="_blank">Mount Sinai study</a></span></div><div><br /></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;
