font-family: arial; font-size: small;">Excerpted from the first letter to group:</span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #222222; font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #222222; font-family: arial;">When Mike got sick back in January 2022, we continued to go out and about in the city. Our reasoning was that it\'s better than staying home, and it passed time while waiting for the symptoms to resolve. As you all might know by now, through doctor visits, much research, and two attempts at meds with egregious outcomes, the neuropsychiatric symptoms never resolved.</span></div><div style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #222222; font-family: arial; font-size: small;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Fast forward to August 5 2022 when we started over with a new psychiatrist and new meds. This new psychiatrist agreed about Mike going on those outings, so we continued our city trips.&nbsp;</span></div><div style="color: #222222;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Some thoughts about our trips:</span></div><div style="color: #222222;"><ol><li style="color: black;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><span face="arial, sans-serif">Mike does not enjoy the trips (he doesn\'t enjoy anything) but they don\'t make his condition worse. Before August, they were slightly better than a "wash." That\'s because before August, while the anxiety was high (and depression lower)</span>&nbsp;he was getting some slight relief from the anxiety from being in motion on the train and while walking. So we had been doing lots of trains and lots of walking.</span></li><li style="color: black;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Now that the anxiety dropped and the depression rose, being in motion doesn\'t give him any relief at all, but we keep going out because it\'s still better than not doing so.</span></li><li style="color: black;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Sometimes the outings are just to accompany me to work. We travel together, then during my two hour shift, he sits on a bench and reads. We are thankful that he can concentrate on a book.<br /></span></li><li style="color: black;"><span style="font-family: arial;">When we\'re on an outing, I sometimes take pictures and post them on Facebook. He often smiles for the camera but it doesn\'t mean anything. He\'s an empty shell. I\'ve learned that it is not atypical for depressed persons to look and act "normal." We try to keep that need to a minimum, because "acting normal" takes precious energy, of which he has so little.&nbsp;</span></li><li><span face="arial, sans-serif"><span style="color: black; font-family: arial;">Those smiles do mean something, though. If we get a good feeling from seeing him smile, perhaps that\'s because it offers memories of the past Mike and hopes for the future Mike. It reminds us that Mike is "in there somewhere." So if you\'re inclined to say "but he looks so good," it\'s an interesting dichotomy -- the smile does not reflect his condition, but it does something&nbsp;good and positive for all those who love him. And, in my opinion, that\'s valid!</span></span></li></ol><div><span style="color: black; font-family: arial;">All of you have your own busy lives and full plates. So I can\'t help repeating myself when I thank folks for being on this email list. Whatever amount you want to "take in" is great. Even just having my writings land in your email is good enough to motivate me to write. Writing helps me as his an advocate and researcher.</span></div></div><div><br style="background-color: white; color: #222222; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;" /></div>'}, {'url': 'http://www.longcovidmind.info/2022/08/the-graph.html', 'title': '22-08-31 The Graph', 'content': '<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjuzrzNAZCBOfPG44bpUDel08BHcjKtgDcely6AX7IroJT4J2mhLJLDtbNUqAJ3JvAjf9YfaqPKYdmJItQe02MJZ6VD6JqONo-CtRitIqNQY4BoA1LzYdrqnLLwVWVrwX134qVHXyzWXBTsjkyOr9BfEarPNAtqatcjRR_7_IZ7ZSyfAK8-5x8g-lnoIw/s1650/22-08-31%20Mike\'s%20graph387.jpg" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1650" data-original-width="1275" height="400" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjuzrzNAZCBOfPG44bpUDel08BHcjKtgDcely6AX7IroJT4J2mhLJLDtbNUqAJ3JvAjf9YfaqPKYdmJItQe02MJZ6VD6JqONo-CtRitIqNQY4BoA1LzYdrqnLLwVWVrwX134qVHXyzWXBTsjkyOr9BfEarPNAtqatcjRR_7_IZ7ZSyfAK8-5x8g-lnoIw/w309-h400/22-08-31%20Mike\'s%20graph387.jpg" width="309" /></a></div><span style="font-family: arial;">I started this graph in August, after going back through my written notes from Mike. The bulk of this graph, as you can see on the bottom is August 2022.<br /><br />From January 2022 to August 2022, it was very steady, so there was no need for the graph. The depression was 30 with daily gusts up to 70. There were also a total of three depression gusts to 90. In contrast, the anxiety had been very steady at 90.<br /><br />As you can see, everything changed in August when we got the new doctor and he started some new meds. You will see that the anxiety plummeted, but the depression rose.<br /><br />The scale is based on "patient report." That is, every morning, Mike gives me status of his depression and anxiety, in the form of numbers from 0&nbsp; to 100.<br /><br />We are also writing up the PHQ-9 Questionnaire on a weekly basis. Both assessments serve to inform the doctor of changes, correlations, and patterns.</span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span><p><br /></p>'}, {'url': 'http://www.longcovidmind.info/2022/08/letter-to-larger-group-on-august-31.html', 'title': '22-08-31 Returning to work', 'content': '<p><span style="color: #222222;"></span></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiuG2xl2se3ng8f6jiDVeihvDuj95Qh4zlhsXUUtVl0W_hGA8x7IXHgZZjR_oAd4a_bnxnr90xb1Lwlj2GJ31KiUODwcVj1B6rJCN9Fqj9EEMBr2wtnDEaKt2aJbd9OtDvrptI2oxhdkWwc5W2C1-7ZsISaB0djOBMX91Djz2jnc5RvbbXy4skgPlT8xw/s2000/funny-tired-man-sleeping-his-desk-laptop-after-hard-work-day-office-vector-cartoon_376504-927.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="2000" data-original-width="1996" height="200" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiuG2xl2se3ng8f6jiDVeihvDuj95Qh4zlhsXUUtVl0W_hGA8x7IXHgZZjR_oAd4a_bnxnr90xb1Lwlj2GJ31KiUODwcVj1B6rJCN9Fqj9EEMBr2wtnDEaKt2aJbd9OtDvrptI2oxhdkWwc5W2C1-7ZsISaB0djOBMX91Djz2jnc5RvbbXy4skgPlT8xw/w199-h200/funny-tired-man-sleeping-his-desk-laptop-after-hard-work-day-office-vector-cartoon_376504-927.jpg" width="199" /></a><span style="color: #222222;"></span></div><span style="color: #222222; font-family: arial;">Excerpted from the second letter to group:</span><p></p><p><span style="font-family: arial;">Hi all. Today is Wednesday. This email list has grown, hence the blind copy. We are really feeling the love. Well okay, I\'m feeling the love. Mike, somewhere inside his spirit, beneath the depression, is registering the love.</span></p><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Anyhow, the last email was on Saturday August 27. It was about how Dr.&nbsp;Vijal&nbsp;Parikh\'s next prescription for Mike was to go back to work, and that\'s not because Mike is all better, but because it was the right time for infusing change. Mike didn\'t have any interest in doing so, but sometimes we have to resort to the good old fashioned "listen to the doc." And besides, my own blink moment told me it was correct.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">So here\'s an updated status, which I\'ll write in a list:</span></div><div><ol><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">For over a week now, his anxiety has been very steady at a 10 and his depression has been pretty steady at 60. Attached is today\'s graph</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">The 20 mg THC edibles do the job of lowering his depression significantly enough to give him relief, but he can\'t get any work done. In fact, if he does them in the evening, he can\'t work the next day. So he\'s still figuring out when he can take the edibles, which might be largely on weekends. (The "figuring out" is a daily task for both of us regarding this illness. We\'re always chasing it.)</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">He started work on Sunday, with some nervousness, but through discussion that morning, we were able to identify that the nervousness was of the garden variety --&nbsp; that is, anyone going back to the&nbsp; business they own, in this volatile economy, after being completely out of touch, is going to be a bit nervous. That is, it wasn\'t anxiety. It\'s helpful to tease apart feelings from illness.</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">He was also nervous and wondering if he would be able to work at all because that relentless depression is like a wall in front of him. When he was working previously through this nightmare (from January through July) he was dealing with a high level of anxiety and a low level of depression. Now they are swapped, so he just had no idea if he could do it. That nervousness too, was not illness-based.</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">He got through Sunday, but slowly because each new task required new, tiring self-talk to get started. After his workday,&nbsp; he comes out of his office and pours himself into his recliner at the end.&nbsp;There\'s no joy in any part of his day and he has nothing leftover after work. He watches game shows on tv. He\'s an empty shell</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Today is Day Four of work. Today is a little different because he got little sleep last night (first time in a while) and he has to start his workday with a doctor visit to the city. So today will give us a new data point.</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">He\'s now getting used to the idea that much of his work efforts each day are directed toward his self-talk to make himself get through the day. As for the content of his brain, it seems to be okay, but he has his doubts. He still can reason and problem-solve but he lacks self-confidence now. It\'s all part of the stinkin\' illness.</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">We\'re solid now about the reason why the anxiety is down -- it\'s because the Gabapentin is working well. Some patients with anxiety respond to Gabapentin this quickly, so no surprise there. Still no serious side effects.<br /></span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">As for the depression, that could still take up to four more weeks, that is, if the Luvox does its job. Still no serious side effects.</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">If the Luvox doesn\'t do its job, Dr. Parikh has in his head approximately eight more steps (LOL) to try over time. Mike won\'t get dropped as a patient this time.&nbsp;</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">I\'m guessing because of how taxing it is for him to work, he might be resting all this weekend</span></li></ol><div><span style="font-family: arial;">I could keep on writing and writing. So I\'m arbitrarily stopping. I don\'t want to lose my readers with too much prose and lists.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Mike used to love his job. It\'s his own company; he created it; he hired everyone there. I look forward to the future with hope that he can love his job again. And I look forward to the day when his smiles for the camera, when I\'m dragging him around the city for his mental health, are real.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">All of you have your own full plate. I\'m going to list a few reasons why:</span><p></p><div><div><ol><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">So little is known about Long Covid, except in small pockets. Even Mike\'s new psychiatrist, who is amazing and who knows Long Covid, is on the leading edge. So we are on the leading edge too. Thus we want to document our journey</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Within Long Covid, our situation represents yet a smaller population, as Mike\'s symptoms are pretty much limited to the neuropsychiatric (depression, anxiety, brain fog, memory loss, suicidal ideations, and some psychosis)</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">We want others to speak freely and to spread the word about the seriousness of Long Covid. Mental health issues need to be out in the open. It might even help someone who currently has neuropsychiatric symptoms, and they don\'t even know it\'s connected to having had Covid. Some of them might have even had silent Covid. We know two such people in our own little circle who, when we described what happened to Mike, had that moment of connecting the dots about their own conditions. So speak freely with others all you want about our journey.</span></li><li style="margin-left: 15px;"><span style="font-family: arial;">As Mike\'s caregiver, I have to keep feeding my mental own health. Mike is not working any more, and the fate of the business is unknown. Mike\'s condition had gotten worse, not better, in July.&nbsp; And so he had to go on disability. He went from impaired to despair. For a week or two, I was looking for in-patient placements in a treatment center. That didn\'t pan out, as they are filled with folks with substance abuse issues, and just the tip of the iceberg of folks who have what Mike has. The covid-specialized treatment centers have year-long waiting lists, and they mostly treat the more physical symptoms.</span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">I\'ve learned more than I\'d like about how isolating it is to have a chronic illness. The reason it\'s isolating is because after a while, friends and loved ones tend to fall away in frustration. It\'s human nature to do so. I\'m doing everything I can to prevent that from happening, as we have no timetable.</span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">In any case, Mike\'s condition now has a name and a diagnosis code, so I guess we could call that progress (omg).</span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">It\'s called&nbsp;Post-Acute Sequelae of SARS CoV-2 infection (PASC). The diagnosis code is&nbsp;ICD-10 code U09.9 Post COVID-19 condition, unspecified. It was announced by the CDC in July. That\'s how newly emerging this is, and it also helps explain why it\'s been, so far, downplayed, misunderstood, and even denigrated by both the medical community and the general population.</span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">I\'ve been Mike\'s advocate, Case Manager, companion, social worker, researchist, and therapist. To make a long story short, his therapist dropped him as a patient. It takes months to get another one, and almost no therapists are up on this condition.&nbsp;</span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">But we did find a way to get a new therapist -- by getting one who doesn\'t take insurance. So as of twelve days ago, he has a new therapist whom we are paying for out of pocket, and who has prescribed yet another medication. This new therapist actually knows about PASC. That leaves me still as Mike\'s researcher and advocate (fewer hats than before.)</span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">Right now, Maddie is with us for a week. Also Dwight is now living with us. So this week, I\'m getting some relief. Maddie is taking Mike this evening for his MRI (another long story.) So many subplots in this.</span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div style="color: #222222; text-align: left;"><span style="font-family: arial;">I\'ve realized I need to start reaching out more to our support group, so I\'m beginning that project, alongside the Mike-projects I\'m already working on.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div style="color: #222222; She told us this would take a few days instead of a few months</span></li><li><span style="font-family: arial;">Mike\'s GP did as promised, and we started seeing an outstanding psychiatrist. I like this group a lot, but they knew nothing about these tests. It\'s another way the Brits are ahead of us. Sad but true.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">This had become a critical issue because the first two meds that Mike tried had such severe side effects that he developed trauma, and the side effects lasted so long that it was clear he could not use those meds.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Had he had the Genesight test, he could avoided months of pain and months of delay in getting better.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">We contacted our GP\'s who were open to learning about these new tests. Our practice had to then register as a Genesight clinic before they can order the tests for us. That process took a few weeks, but it proved well worth the wait.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">Mike\'s Genesight results showed clearly that the two psychotropic meds he had already tried were a bad idea for his genetic makeup.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">At that time, we still had the first psychologist, who did not make a good recommendation, even with Mike\'s Genesight report in front of him.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">But when we started over with the new, excellent psychiatrist, Dr.&nbsp;Vijal&nbsp;Parikh, he prescribed properly, and was already knowledgeable about Genesight reports.</span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-family: arial;">I got a Genesight test too, and it was clear from mine why the most conventional SSRI\'s work fine for me. I\'ve back dated it to May 20 because that\'s when I resumed SSRI\'s.<div><br /></div><div>I had been off SSRI\'s for two years before that, but after getting Covid, my anxiety crept back, and got worse than it\'s ever been before.</div><div><br /></div><div>My body\'s experience of anxiety is different from what Mike experiences. That\'s what I had for months.</div><div><br /></div><div>So by May I was back on SSRI\'s. It\'s back dated to April 14, the day Mike had his Focused Ultrasound non-invasive brain surgery:</div><script>var pfHeaderImgUrl = \'\';var pfHeaderTagline = \'\';var pfdisableClickToDel = 0;var pfHideImages = 1;var pfImageDisplayStyle = \'none\';var pfDisablePDF = 1;var pfDisableEmail = 1;var pfDisablePrint = 0;var pfCustomCSS = \'\';var pfBtVersion=\'2\';(function(){var js,pf;pf=document.createElement(\'script\');pf.type=\'text/javascript\';pf.src=\'//cdn.printfriendly.com/printfriendly.js\';document.getElementsByTagName(\'head\')[0].appendChild(pf)})();</script><div><br /></div>Unrelated to and long before Covid, Mike had a deteriorating condition called Essential Tremor Disorder.<div><br /><div>It seemed to worsen greatly in 2021, and that\'s when we found out there\'s a new treatment for it that involves sending ultrasound signals to the brain for three hours while in an MRI machine.</div><div><br /></div><div>It took us a year to get it all set up, and at last, we had a surgery date for April 2022. The fact that Mike had been suffering from Long Covid neurological symptoms did not deter us, as it could take months to reschedule the appointment.</div><div><br /></div><div>His condition was such that his right hand shakiness rendered it almost useless, and his left hand shakiness was getting worse due to his dependence upon it to assist his right hand.</div><div><br /></div><div>He was assured by the surgeon that, although he would get no anesthesia so that he could respond to commands in real time, he would feel no pain.</div><div><br /></div><div>He did feel pain. In addition, the doctor had to work a great deal harder to get it to work. We now know that had Mike not had this particular doctor and instead had some other doctor who "knew" the procedure, the procedure might have failed.</div><div><br /></div><div>As it turns out, the procedure was wildly successful. At the present time, insurance does not cover treatment on the other hand, but Mike doesn\'t even think he will need it because the left hand is now far less pressured to assist the right.</div><div><br /></div><div>We wonder today if the reason he felt pain which was so unusual, had something to do with his existing Long Covid condition. After all, we know that Long Covid causes brain swelling.</div><div><br /></div><div>This is one of those questions we may never have the answer to. But we are thrilled with the results of the Focused Ultrasound. He can now do normal daily tasks.</div><div><br /></div><div><br /></div></div>'}]
